37 "§ 58-64A-95. Expansion entrance fees and deposits.
38 All entrance fees and deposits collected for independent living units in an expansion requiring
39 Commissioner approval under this Part shall be placed in an escrow account in accordance with
40 Part 4 of this Article unless otherwise exempted by the Commissioner.
41 "Part 4. Escrow Account.
42 "§ 58-64A-100. Escrow account required.
43 All entrance fees and deposits, when required by this Article, shall be deposited by the
44 provider in an escrow account and shall be maintained in a segregated account without any
45 commingling with other funds, including any funds or accounts owned by the provider. The
46 escrow agent and all terms governing an escrow account shall be approved in advance by the
47 Commissioner.
48 "§ 58-64A-105. Escrow agreement requirements.
49 The escrow agreement between an applicant or a provider and the escrow agent shall be in
50 writing and include, in addition to any other provisions required by law, all of the following:
Page 20 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (1) A provision requiring that all funds received shall be placed into the escrow
2 account in accordance with G.S. 58-64A-115.
3 (2) A provision for investment of escrow account funds in a manner consistent
4 with G.S. 58-64A-120.
5 (3) A provision regarding the payment of interest earned on the funds held in the
6 escrow account in the manner specified in G.S. 58-64A-125.
7 (4) A provision for refunds to depositors in the manner specified by
8 G.S. 58-64A-135.
9 (5) A provision that any refund or release of escrow account funds be performed
10 in the manner specified in G.S. 58-64A-135 and G.S. 58-64A-140, including
11 a statement as to whom payment of interest earned on the funds will be made.
12 (6) A statement that the purpose of the escrow agreement is to protect residents
13 and prospective residents.
14 (7) The amount of the escrow agent fee.
15 (8) A provision that funds deposited shall not be subject to any liens or charges
16 by the escrow agent.
17 (9) A provision requiring the escrow agent to furnish the provider with a monthly
18 statement indicating the amount of any disbursements from or deposits to the
19 escrow account and the condition of the account during the monthly period
20 covered by the statement.
21 (10) A provision requiring the escrow agent to furnish to the Commissioner, upon
22 the request of the Commissioner, periodic reports, including the monthly
23 statement required pursuant to subdivision (9) of this section, certifying the
24 amount of funds held on deposit.
25 (11) A provision requiring the escrow agent to furnish to a depositor, upon the
26 request of a depositor, a statement indicating the depositor's portion of the
27 escrow account.
28 (12) Representations by the escrow agent that it is not and shall not be during the
29 term of the escrow agreement, a related party of the provider, a lender to the
30 provider, or a fiduciary for any lender or bondholder for the provider, unless
31 approved by the Commissioner.
32 "§ 58-64A-110. Changes to escrow agreement.
33 All changes to an escrow agreement shall be submitted to, and approved by, the
34 Commissioner before use by a provider.
35 "§ 58-64A-115. Entrance fee and deposit delivery to the escrow agent.
36 (a) The provider shall deliver to the escrow agent any entrance fees or deposits required
37 to be maintained in an escrow account pursuant to this Article within 10 business days after
38 receipt by the provider.
39 (b) Any deposit delivery to an escrow agent pursuant to this Article shall be accompanied
40 with a copy of the executed nonbinding reservation agreement, binding reservation agreement,
41 or continuing care contract, a copy of the receipt given to the depositor, a summary of all deposits
42 made on that date, and any other materials required by the escrow agent.
43 "§ 58-64A-120. Investment of funds in escrow.
44 (a) All entrance fees and deposits subject to an escrow agreement under this Article shall
45 be maintained by the escrow agent in one of the following manners:
46 (1) Investment in an interest-bearing account.
47 (2) Investment in instruments guaranteed by the federal government or an agency
48 of the federal government.
49 (3) Investment in investment funds secured by federally guaranteed instruments.
50 (b) Any investment shall not diminish the funds held in escrow below the amounts
51 required by this Article.
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 21

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 "§ 58-64A-125. Earnings from funds in escrow.
2 (a) Interest, income, and other gains derived from funds held in an escrow account shall
3 not be released or distributed from the escrow account except upon written approval of the
4 Commissioner.
5 (b) Approval by the Commissioner for the release of earnings generated from funds held
6 in escrow shall be based upon an assessment that funds remaining in the escrow account meet
7 the requirements of this Article and, if applicable, will be sufficient to pay refunds and any
8 interest promised to all depositors.
9 (c) When release of earnings is approved by the Commissioner, interest earned by the
10 funds in the escrow account shall be distributed to the provider or depositors in accordance with
11 the terms of the continuing care contract, binding reservation agreement, or nonbinding
12 reservation agreement.
13 "§ 58-64A-130. Escrowed funds not to be used as collateral.
14 No funds held in an escrow account shall be encumbered or used as collateral for any
15 obligation of the provider, or any other person, unless the provider obtains prior written approval
16 from the Commissioner for the encumbrance or use as collateral. The Commissioner shall not
17 approve any encumbrance or use as collateral under this section unless the encumbrance or use
18 as collateral is expressly subordinated to the rights of depositors under this Article to refunds of
19 their entrance fees or deposits.
20 "§ 58-64A-135. Refunds of escrowed entrance fees and deposits.
21 (a) An escrow agent shall refund to a depositor, or their legal representative, all amounts
22 required by the depositor's nonbinding reservation agreement, binding reservation agreement, or
23 continuing care contract upon receiving written notice from the provider of any of the following:
24 (1) The death of a depositor.
25 (2) Nonacceptance by the provider.
26 (3) Voluntary cancellation.
27 (4) The denial of an application pursuant to this Article.
28 (5) Written notice from the Commissioner.
29 (b) Refunds required in subsection (a) of this section shall be paid within 10 business
30 days after the escrow agent receives the written notice described in subsection (a) of this section.
31 (c) If voluntary cancellation of a continuing care contract or a binding reservation
32 agreement occurs after construction of the continuing care retirement community or expansion
33 of a continuing care retirement community has begun, but prior to the independent living unit's
34 initial occupancy, the refund may be delayed until another depositor has reserved a similar
35 independent living unit and paid the necessary entrance fee or deposit. This delay shall not exceed
36 one year, unless the time period is extended by the Commissioner upon a showing of good cause
37 by the provider.
38 "§ 58-64A-140. Release of escrowed entrance fees and deposits.
39 (a) To request a release of the first twenty-five percent (25%) of each escrowed entrance
40 fee and deposit, a provider shall petition in writing to the Commissioner and certify all of the
41 following:
42 (1) The provider has presold at least fifty percent (50%) of the proposed
43 independent living units, having received a minimum ten percent (10%)
44 deposit of the total of each applicable entrance fee and placed it in escrow.
45 Any independent living unit for which a refund is pending shall not be counted
46 toward the fifty percent (50%) requirement.
47 (2) The provider has long-term financing in place for the proposed continuing
48 care retirement community or expansion, or if the provider is leasing the land
49 or other real property of the continuing care retirement community,
50 certification that the lease is in place and, if applicable, that the lease has been
51 approved by the Commissioner pursuant to G.S. 58-64A-25.
Page 22 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (3) For a proposed continuing care retirement community, the aggregate entrance
2 fees received or receivable by the provider pursuant to binding reservation
3 agreements and continuing care contracts, plus the anticipated proceeds of any
4 first mortgage loan or other long-term financing commitment, plus any equity
5 being contributed by the provider or a related party, are equal to not less than
6 ninety percent (90%) of the following amount: (i) the aggregate cost of
7 constructing or purchasing, equipping, and furnishing the proposed continuing
8 care retirement community, plus (ii) not less than ninety percent (90%) of the
9 funds estimated to be necessary to fund start-up losses and to reasonably
10 assure full performance of the provider's future continuing care obligations,
11 as reported in the statement of cash flows required by
12 G.S. 58-64A-150(a)(37).
13 (b) To request a release of the remaining seventy-five percent (75%) of escrowed
14 entrance fees and deposits, a provider shall petition in writing to the Commissioner and certify
15 all of the following:
16 (1) The provider has presold at least seventy percent (70%) of the proposed
17 independent living units, having received a minimum ten percent (10%)
18 deposit of each applicable entrance fee and maintains at least seventy-five
19 percent (75%) of each entrance fee or deposit received in escrow, or has
20 maintained an independent living unit occupancy minimum of seventy percent
21 (70%) for at least 60 days. Any independent living unit for which a refund is
22 pending shall not be counted toward the seventy percent (70%) requirement.
23 (2) Construction or purchase of the independent living units has been completed
24 and an occupancy permit, if applicable, has been issued by the local
25 government having authority to issue those permits.
26 (3) The independent living units are available for occupancy by the new residents.
27 (c) The Commissioner shall instruct the escrow agent in writing to release to the provider
28 entrance fees and deposits in the escrow account only when the Commissioner has confirmed the
29 information provided by the provider pursuant to subsection (a) or subsection (b) of this section.
30 (d) The escrow agent shall release the entrance fees and deposits held in the escrow
31 account to the provider only when the Commissioner has instructed it to do so in writing.
32 (e) When a provider discloses in an application that construction will be completed and
33 commence operating in different phases, the Commissioner shall apply the requirements in
34 subsections (a) and (b) of this section to any one or group of phases requested by the provider,
35 provided the provider demonstrates in the prospective financial statements filed with the
36 application that the phase or group of phases is financially viable without the need for any
37 additional phases.
38 (f) For the purposes of this section, a refund is pending if a depositor has canceled a
39 continuing care contract or a binding reservation agreement but has not yet received a refund,
40 either because of timing or because another depositor has not reserved a similar independent
41 living unit and paid the necessary entrance fee or deposit in order to trigger a refund to the
42 canceling depositor.
43 "Part 5. Disclosure Statement.
44 "§ 58-64A-145. Definitions.
45 The following definitions apply to this Part:
46 (1) Adjusted net operating margin ratio. – A profitability ratio that measures the
47 margin generated from the core operations of a provider and net cash proceeds
48 from entrance fees. The quotient shall be calculated by dividing the sum of
49 resident operating income and net proceeds from entrance fees by the sum of
50 resident revenue and net cash proceeds from entrance fees.
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 23

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (2) Average daily cash operating expenses. – The total expenses of a provider
2 incurred in the conduct of the provider's business over a defined period of
3 time, divided by the number of days in that period. For purposes of this
4 definition, "total expenses" includes interest expense, but excludes
5 depreciation expense, amortization expense, realized or unrealized
6 nonoperating losses or expenses, bad debt expense, and other noncash
7 expenses.
8 (3) Capital expenditures as a percentage of depreciation ratio. – A capital
9 structure ratio that indicates the level of capital reinvestment by a provider.
10 The quotient shall be computed by dividing total purchases of property, plant,
11 and equipment by total depreciation expense.
12 (4) Cushion ratio. – A liquidity ratio that measures a provider's ability to pay its
13 annual debt service using its unrestricted cash and investments. The quotient
14 shall be computed by dividing unrestricted cash and investments by annual
15 debt service.
16 (5) Days cash on hand ratio. – A liquidity ratio that measures the number of days
17 of cash operating expenses a provider could cover using its existing
18 unrestricted cash and investments. The quotient shall be computed by dividing
19 unrestricted cash and investments by average daily cash operating expenses.
20 (6) Multi-entity organization. – A collection of distinct legal entities that are
21 under common control.
22 (7) Net operating margin ratio. – A profitability ratio that measures the margin
23 generated from the core operations of a provider. The quotient shall be
24 calculated by dividing resident operating income by resident revenue.
25 (8) Operating ratio. – A profitability ratio that measures whether current year cash
26 operating revenues are sufficient to cover current year cash operating
27 expenses without the inclusion of cash from entrance fee receipts. The
28 quotient shall be computed by dividing total operating expenses, excluding
29 depreciation expense and amortization expense, by total operating revenues,
30 excluding amortization of entrance fees and other deferred revenue.
31 (9) Resale fee. – A contractual assessment by the provider against the proceeds
32 from the sale of an independent living unit.
33 (10) Resident expense. – Total operating expenses excluding interest expense,
34 depreciation expense, amortization expense, and income taxes.
35 (11) Resident revenue. – Total operating revenue excluding interest and dividend
36 income, entrance fee amortization, and contributions.
37 (12) Unrestricted cash and investments. – The sum of the provider's unrestricted
38 cash, cash equivalents and investments, and any provider restricted funds that
39 are available to pay debt or to pay operating expenses. For purposes of this
40 definition, the assets serving as the operating reserve required by
41 G.S. 58-64A-245 shall be considered unrestricted.
42 (13) Unrestricted cash and investments to long-term debt ratio. – A capital
43 structure ratio that (i) measures a provider's position in available cash and
44 marketable securities in relation to its long-term debt and (ii) measures a
45 provider's ability to withstand annual fluctuations in cash. The quotient shall
46 be calculated by dividing unrestricted cash and investments by total long-term
47 debt, less the current portion of long-term debt.
48 "§ 58-64A-150. Disclosure statement.
49 (a) A provider shall prepare a disclosure statement for each continuing care retirement
50 community operated or to be operated in this State that includes all of the following information:
Page 24 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (1) The name, business address, and telephone number of the provider and a

5 nonprofit, the provision of the federal Internal Revenue Code under which the
6 provider is exempt from the payment of income tax, and a statement disclosing
7 whether the provider is current on all tax filings.

9 owned.

50 "§ 58-64A-155. Required delivery of disclosure statement.
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 31

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (a) A provider shall deliver a current disclosure statement meeting the requirements of
2 G.S. 58-64A-150 to the person or the person's legal representative with whom a binding
3 reservation agreement, continuing care contract, or continuing care at home contract is to be
4 entered into. The disclosure statement shall be delivered no later than the earliest of the following
5 occurrences: (i) the execution of a binding reservation agreement, continuing care contract, or
6 continuing care at home contract, or (ii) the transfer of any money or other consideration, other
7 than a nonbinding reservation agreement deposit, to a provider by or on behalf of a prospective
8 resident. For purposes of this subsection, a disclosure statement is current if (i) it is dated within
9 one year plus 160 days prior to the date of delivery and (ii) it is the most recently recorded
10 disclosure statement on file with the Commissioner.
11 (b) The delivery required by this section may be by electronic means if the provider
12 obtains the written consent of the person with whom the binding reservation agreement,
13 continuing care contract, or continuing care at home contract is to be entered into. For the
14 purposes of this subsection, delivery by electronic means shall mean delivery by either of the
15 following methods:
16 (1) Delivery to an electronic mail address at which the person has consented to
17 receive the disclosure statement.
18 (2) Both of the following:
19 a. Posting the disclosure statement on an electronic network or site
20 accessible by the internet through use of a mobile application,
21 computer, mobile device, tablet, or any other electronic device.
22 b. Sending separate notice of the posting described in sub-subdivision a.
23 of this subdivision to the electronic mail address at which the person
24 consented to receive notice of the disclosure statement posting.
25 (c) After receiving delivery of a disclosure statement pursuant to this section, a
26 prospective resident shall sign an acknowledgement of receipt. The acknowledgement shall
27 include (i) the date, (ii) the name of the person signing, and (iii) the date of the disclosure
28 statement received, including date revised, if any. The provider shall provide a copy of the
29 acknowledgement of receipt to the person signing and shall maintain the original. The
30 acknowledgement of receipt required by this subsection may be received, given, and maintained
31 in either an electronic or paper form.
32 (d) A copy of all disclosure statements, including all amendments, filed with and
33 recorded by the Commissioner shall be maintained by the provider, in either electronic or paper
34 form, for at least five years.
35 "§ 58-64A-165. Other revisions to disclosure statement.
36 (a) A provider may revise its disclosure statement at any time if, in the opinion of the
37 provider, revision is necessary to prevent an otherwise current disclosure statement from
38 containing a material misstatement of fact or omitting a material fact required to be stated therein.
39 A provider that revises its disclosure statement for this purpose shall submit the revised disclosure
40 statement to the Commissioner before delivery of the disclosure statement to any resident or
41 prospective resident.
42 (b) If a disclosure statement is revised in accordance with this section or
43 G.S. 58-64A-150(g), the cover page shall additionally be revised to reflect the revision date.
44 (c) Within five business days of receipt of a revised disclosure statement pursuant to this
45 section, the Commissioner shall notify the provider in writing that the revised disclosure
46 statement has been received and recorded and is considered to be the current disclosure statement
47 for purposes of this Article. After sending this notification, the Commissioner shall post the
48 revised disclosure statement on the Department's website within five business days. After
49 receiving the Commissioner's notification, a provider revising its disclosure statement pursuant
50 to this section shall make the revised disclosure statement available to all residents either in
51 electronic or paper form.

1 "Part 6. Binding Reservation Agreement and Continuing Care Contract.
2 "§ 58-64A-170. Binding reservation agreement.
3 A binding reservation agreement shall include all of the following:
4 (1) A provision that the person entering into the agreement may rescind the
5 agreement within 30 days following the later of the following occurrences: (i)
6 the execution of the agreement or (ii) the receipt of a disclosure statement that
7 meets the requirements of G.S. 58-64A-150.
8 (2) A provision that the agreement shall be automatically canceled if either of the
9 following occurs: (i) a depositor dies before signing a continuing care contract
10 or (ii) a depositor would be precluded from signing a continuing care contract
11 and occupying a living unit in the continuing care retirement community under
12 the terms of a continuing care contract due to illness, injury, or incapacity.
13 (3) A provision that, if an agreement is rescinded, automatically canceled, or
14 otherwise canceled by the depositor, the depositor shall receive a refund of all
15 money or other consideration transferred to the provider. All of the following
16 shall be deducted from the depositor's refund:
17 a. Nonstandard costs specifically incurred by the provider at the request
18 of the depositor and described in the agreement.
19 b. Any nonrefundable fees specifically set forth in the agreement.
20 c. Any service charge specifically set forth in the agreement that shall
21 not exceed the greater of (i) three thousand dollars ($3,000) or (ii) two
22 percent (2%) of the entrance fee. In no event shall the service charge
23 exceed the amount of consideration transferred to the provider by the
24 depositor or a service charge be assessed due to the termination of the
25 agreement because of the failure of the provider to meet its obligations
26 under the agreement, or upon the failure of the provider to obtain a
27 permanent license in accordance with this Article.
28 (4) A provision that any refund due to a depositor for a cancellation or termination
29 for reasons not provided for in this section shall be computed in accordance
30 with the terms of the agreement.
31 "§ 58-64A-175. Continuing care contract.
32 (a) A continuing care contract shall include all of the following:
33 (1) A provision that the person contracting with the provider may rescind the
34 contract within 30 days following the later of (i) the execution of the contract
35 or (ii) the receipt of a disclosure statement that meets the requirements of
36 G.S. 58-64A-150, and a resident to whom the contract pertains is not required
37 to move into the continuing care retirement community before the expiration
38 of the 30-day period.
39 (2) A provision that, if a resident dies before occupying a living unit in the
40 continuing care retirement community, or if, on account of illness, injury, or
41 incapacity, a resident would be precluded from occupying a living unit in the
42 continuing care retirement community under the terms of the contract, the
43 contract is automatically canceled.
44 (3) A provision that, for rescinded or canceled contracts under this subsection and
45 contracts canceled before a living unit is initially available for occupancy by
46 the first resident of a living unit, the resident or the resident's legal
47 representative, shall receive a refund of all money or other consideration
48 transferred to the provider, less (i) periodic fees specified in the contract and
49 applicable only to the period a living unit was actually occupied by the
50 resident; (ii) those nonstandard costs specifically incurred by the provider at
51 the request of the resident and described in the contract or any contract
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 33

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 amendment signed by the resident; (iii) nonrefundable fees, if set out in the
2 contract; and (iv) a reasonable service charge, if set out in the contract, not to
3 exceed the greater of three thousand dollars ($3,000) or two percent (2%) of
4 the entrance fee. In no event shall the service charge exceed the amount of
5 consideration transferred to the provider by the resident, or a service charge
6 be assessed due to the termination of the contract because of the failure of the
7 provider to meet its obligations under the contract, or upon the failure of the
8 provider to obtain a permanent license in accordance with this Article.
9 (4) A provision that any refund due to a resident for a cancellation or termination
10 for reasons not provided for in this section shall be computed in accordance
11 with the terms of the contract.
12 (b) A continuing care contract shall specify all of the following:
13 (1) All fees required of residents, including any entrance fee and any ongoing
14 periodic fees.
15 (2) The services to be provided.
16 (3) The policy regarding changing the resident's living unit, if necessary, for the
17 protection of the health or safety of the resident or the general and economic
18 welfare of other residents.
19 (4) The policies to be implemented if the resident cannot pay the periodic fees.
20 (5) The terms governing the refund of any portion of the entrance fee in the event
21 of death or cancellation by the resident or provider.
22 (6) The policy regarding increasing the periodic fees.
23 (7) A description of the living unit.
24 (8) Any property rights of the resident.
25 (9) The policy, if any, regarding periodic fee adjustments if the resident is absent
26 from the continuing care retirement community.
27 (10) Any requirement that the resident maintain long-term care insurance or apply
28 for Medicaid benefits or any other public assistance program.
29 (c) A continuing care contract shall include the following notice immediately above the
30 contract signature line and be in type that is boldfaced, capitalized, underlined, or otherwise set
31 out from the surrounding written material so as to be conspicuous:
32 "NOTICE
33
34 Because the authority to enter into continuing care contracts granted by the North Carolina
35 Department of Insurance is neither a guarantee of performance by the provider nor an
36 endorsement of any continuing care contract provision, prospective residents must carefully
37 consider the risks, benefits, and costs before signing a continuing care contract and are strongly
38 encouraged to seek financial and legal advice before doing so."
39 "Part 7. Continuing Care at Home.
40 "§ 58-64A-180. Home care services defined.
41 As used is this Part, "home care services" is defined in G.S. 131E-136.
42 "§ 58-64A-185. Application.
43 (a) No person shall arrange or provide continuing care at home unless licensed by the
44 Commissioner pursuant to this Article. Only a provider who has obtained a permanent license or
45 a restricted permanent license pursuant to this Article may apply to the Commissioner for a
46 continuing care at home license. The application shall include all of the following:
47 (1) An application fee of five hundred dollars ($500.00).
48 (2) A draft amended disclosure statement containing a description of the proposed
49 continuing care at home program, including the primary market area to be
50 served, the types of services to be provided, and the fees to be charged.
51 (3) A copy of the proposed continuing care at home contract.
Page 34 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (4) An actuarial study prepared in accordance with accepted actuarial standards
2 of practice which estimates when the continuing care at home program is
3 projected to be in satisfactory actuarial balance. Providers who do not collect
4 entrance fees or some other type of up-front prepayment of costs are exempt
5 from this requirement and shall only be required to submit an actuarial
6 projection of future population flows and adult care home bed and nursing bed
7 needs using appropriate mortality, morbidity, withdrawal, occupancy, and
8 other demographic assumptions, and using a projection period that extends to
9 a point at which, in the actuary's professional judgment, the use of a longer
10 period would not materially affect the results and conclusions.
11 (5) A market study prepared by a person experienced in the preparation of market
12 studies for continuing care at home or similar programs that demonstrates
13 sufficient interest in a continuing care at home program.
14 (6) Prospective financial statements prepared by an independent certified public
15 accountant that show the financial impact of providing continuing care at
16 home on the provider and the continuing care retirement community. The
17 prospective financial statements shall include a statement of activities
18 reporting the revenue and expense details for providing continuing care at
19 home, as well as the impact the program will have on the operations of the
20 provider and the continuing care retirement community, including the
21 operating reserve.
22 (7) Evidence of the license required under Part 3 of Article 6 of Chapter 131E of
23 the General Statutes to provide home care services, or a contract with a
24 licensed home care agency for the provision of home care services to be
25 provided to residents under the continuing care at home program.
26 (b) The Commissioner shall comply with the review schedule in G.S. 58-64A-70 in
27 response to an application for a continuing care at home license.
28 (c) The Commissioner shall approve an application for a continuing care at home license
29 if all of the following requirements are met:
30 (1) The application complies with this section.
31 (2) None of the grounds for denial listed in G.S. 58-64A-280 apply to the
32 applicant.
33 (3) The applicant is able to provide continuing care at home as proposed.
34 (4) There is sufficient consumer interest in the continuing care at home program
35 proposed by the applicant, as evidenced by the market study.
36 (5) The program proposed by the applicant will not have a detrimental financial
37 impact on the applicant and continuing care retirement community, as
38 determined by the Commissioner.
39 (d) After receiving a continuing care at home license, the provider may arrange or provide
40 continuing care at home and shall file an amended disclosure statement with the Commissioner
41 which contains the information regarding continuing care at home required by G.S. 58-64A-150.
42 (e) After the issuance of a continuing care at home license, the Commissioner shall
43 require a provider to submit periodic reports in a form prescribed by the Commissioner to monitor
44 the status of the continuing care at home program.
45 "§ 58-64A-190. Continuing care at home contract.
46 (a) A continuing care at home contract shall include all of the following provisions:
47 (1) A provision that the individual contracting with the provider may rescind the
48 contract within 30 days following the later of (i) the execution of the contract
49 or (ii) the receipt of a disclosure statement that meets the requirements of
50 G.S. 58-64A-150.
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 35

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (2) A provision that, if a resident dies prior to the effective start date of services,
2 or if, on account of illness, injury, or incapacity, a resident would be precluded
3 from meeting the eligibility terms of the contract, the contract is automatically
4 canceled.
5 (3) A provision that, for rescinded or canceled contracts under this subsection, the
6 resident, or the resident's legal representative, shall receive a refund of all
7 money or other consideration transferred to the provider, less (i) periodic fees
8 specified in the contract and applicable only to the period when services were
9 provided to the resident; (ii) nonrefundable fees, if set out in the contract; and
10 (iii) a reasonable service charge, if set out in the contract, not to exceed the
11 greater of three thousand dollars ($3,000) or two percent (2%) of the entrance
12 fee, if any.
13 (4) A provision that any refund due to a resident for any other cancellation or
14 termination not provided for in subdivisions (1) and (2) of this subsection shall
15 be computed in accordance with the terms of the contract.
16 (b) A continuing care at home contract shall specify all of the following:
17 (1) All fees required, including any entrance fee and any ongoing periodic fees.
18 (2) The services to be provided.
19 (3) The policies to be implemented if the resident cannot pay the periodic fees.
20 (4) The terms governing the refund of any portion of the entrance fee in the event
21 of death or cancellation by the resident or provider.
22 (5) The policy regarding the adjustment of periodic fees.
23 (6) Whether transportation will be provided to residents, including travel to and
24 from the continuing care retirement community for services.
25 (7) The mechanism for monitoring residents who live outside the continuing care
26 retirement community.
27 (8) The process that will be followed to establish priority if a resident wishes to
28 exercise the resident's right to move into an independent living unit at a
29 continuing care retirement community operated by the provider.
30 (9) The process the provider will follow if it becomes necessary for the resident
31 to move into a long-term care facility.
32 (10) The policy that will be followed if a resident chooses not to move to a
33 long-term care facility when recommended by the provider.
34 (11) The policy, if any, that would entitle a resident to select placement in a
35 long-term care facility that is not owned and operated by the provider or by a
36 related party of the provider.
37 (12) A statement describing any applicable geographical limits of the continuing
38 care at home program, and the policy that will be followed in the event that a
39 resident relocates to a different residence outside the geographical limits
40 covered by the continuing care at home program.
41 (c) A continuing care at home contract shall include the following notice immediately
42 above the contract signature line and be in type that is boldfaced, capitalized, underlined, or
43 otherwise set out from the surrounding written material so as to be conspicuous:
44 "NOTICE
45
46 Because the authority to enter into continuing care at home contracts granted by the North
47 Carolina Department of Insurance is neither a guarantee of performance by the provider nor an
48 endorsement of any continuing care at home contract provision, prospective residents must
49 carefully consider the risks, benefits, and costs before signing a continuing care at home contract
50 and are strongly encouraged to seek financial and legal advice before doing so."
51 "Part 8. Financial Reporting and Monitoring.
Page 36 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 "§ 58-64A-195. General requirements related to filing and extensions for filing of annual
2 audited financial statements.
3 (a) All providers shall have an annual audit by an independent certified public accountant
4 and shall file audited financial statements with the Commissioner within 150 days following the
5 end of each fiscal year.
6 (b) Extensions of the filing date may be granted by the Commissioner for 30-day periods
7 upon a showing by the provider and its independent certified public accountant of the reasons for
8 requesting an extension and determination by the Commissioner of good cause for an extension.
9 The request for extension must be received in writing not less than 10 days before the due date
10 and in sufficient detail to permit the Commissioner to make an informed decision with respect to
11 the requested extension.
12 (c) If an initial extension is granted in accordance with the provisions in subsection (b)
13 of this section, a similar extension of 30 days is granted for the filing of the provider's annual
14 disclosure statement.
15 "§ 58-64A-200. Contents of annual audited financial statements.
16 (a) The annual audited financial statements shall report the financial position of the
17 provider as of the end of the most recent fiscal year and the results of its operations, cash flows,
18 and changes in equity or net assets for the year then ended. The audited financial statements shall
19 be comparative, presenting the amounts as of the end of the most current year-end and the
20 amounts as of the immediately preceding year-end. However, in the first year in which a provider
21 is required to file audited financial statements, the comparative data may be omitted.
22 (b) The audited financial statements shall include the following:
23 (1) Report of independent certified public accountant.
24 (2) Balance sheet reporting assets, liabilities, and net assets or equity.
25 (3) Statement of operations.
26 (4) Statement of cash flows.
27 (5) Statement of changes in net assets or equity.
28 (6) Notes to financial statements.
29 (c) The audited financial statements shall be prepared in accordance with one of the
30 following requirements:
31 (1) If a provider is required by generally accepted accounting principles to have
32 their financial statements consolidated with other persons, the audited
33 consolidated financial statements shall include a consolidating balance sheet,
34 a consolidating statement of operations and changes in net assets or equity,
35 and a consolidating statement of cash flows as supplemental information to
36 the audited consolidated financial statements. This supplemental information
37 shall also include a statement of operations for each continuing care retirement
38 community operated by the provider under this Article.
39 (2) If the provider includes one or more persons acting in concert to offer and
40 provide continuing care, the audited financial statements shall be combined
41 and shall include a combining balance sheet, a combining statement of
42 operations and changes in net assets or equity, and a combining statement of
43 cash flows as supplemental information to the audited combined financial
44 statements. This supplemental information shall also include a statement of
45 operations for each continuing care retirement community operated by the
46 provider under this Article.
47 (3) If a provider is part of an obligated group, the audited financial statements
48 shall be either consolidated or combined with the other members of the
49 obligated group and shall include a combining or consolidating balance sheet,
50 a combining or consolidating statement of operations and changes in net assets
51 or equity, and a combining or consolidating statement of cash flows as
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 37

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 supplemental information to the audited combined or consolidated financial
2 statements. This supplemental information shall also include a statement of
3 operations for each continuing care retirement community operated by the
4 provider under this Article.
5 (4) If the provider is not required by generally accepted accounting principles to
6 have their financial statements consolidated with other persons, does not
7 include one or more persons acting in concert to offer and provide continuing
8 care, and is not part of an obligated group, then the audited financial
9 statements shall be a stand-alone financial audit of the provider. The audited
10 financial statements must include as supplemental information, if the provider
11 operates more than one continuing care retirement community or has
12 operations that are separate and distinct from the operation of a continuing
13 care retirement community or communities under this Article, a statement of
14 operations for each continuing care retirement community operated by the
15 provider under this Article.
16 (d) If a provider is also licensed to provide continuing care at home, the audited financial
17 statements shall account for the related revenue and expenses generated from the continuing care
18 at home program separate from the provider's other operations when providing the information
19 required by this section.
20 "§ 58-64A-205. Quarterly reporting.
21 Within 45 days after the end of each fiscal quarter, a provider shall file with the
22 Commissioner all of the following:
23 (1) Quarterly unaudited financial statements of the provider and any obligated
24 group of which the provider is a member, which shall include a balance sheet,
25 a statement of operations, and a statement of cash flows, which shall contain
26 the same categories and line items as the annual audited financial statements
27 filed with the Commissioner pursuant to G.S. 58-64A-195.
28 (2) The 12-month daily average occupancy rate by living unit type at each
29 continuing care retirement community operated by the provider in this State
30 in a form prescribed by the Commissioner.
31 (3) Notice of the following:
32 a. Any change in the provider's or the provider's controlling person's
33 board of directors or other governing body, president, chief executive
34 officer, and chief financial officer. Notice shall include the name of
35 the provider, the name of the controlling person, if applicable, the
36 name of the person previously holding the position, the name of the
37 person currently holding the position, a brief biography of the person
38 currently holding the position, and the date the position change took
39 place.
40 b. Any change in the organizational documents of the provider, including
41 changes in the provider's articles of incorporation and bylaws. Copies
42 of the changed documents shall be submitted with the notification to
43 the Commissioner.
44 "§ 58-64A-210. Actuarial study.
45 (a) A provider shall submit to the Commissioner, at least once every three years, an
46 actuarial study prepared in accordance with accepted actuarial standards of practice for each
47 continuing care retirement community operated by the provider in this State and any continuing
48 care at home program that the provider is licensed for pursuant to this Article.
49 (b) If the actuary is unable to form an opinion, or if the opinion is adverse or qualified,
50 the statement of actuarial opinion and the actuarial study shall specifically state the reason.
Page 38 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (c) The Commissioner may request the information required in this section more
2 frequently to assist in the determination of a possible hazardous condition.
3 (d) A provider required to file an actuarial study under this section that held a license on
4 the effective date of this section shall file an actuarial study with the Commissioner before the
5 expiration of three years following the effective date of this section. Thereafter, each provider
6 shall file its required actuarial study before the expiration of three years following the date it last
7 filed an actuarial study with the Commissioner.
8 (e) A provider required to file an actuarial study under this section that did not hold a
9 license on the effective date of this section shall file its first actuarial study within 45 days
10 following the due date for the provider's annual audited financial statements for the fiscal year in
11 which the provider obtained its permanent license. Thereafter, the provider shall file its required
12 actuarial study before the expiration of three years following the date it last filed an actuarial
13 study with the Commissioner.
14 (f) A provider that only offers health care on a fee-for-service basis or only provides a
15 limited discount or limited number of free days in a long-term care facility shall be exempt, unless
16 otherwise required by the Commissioner, from the actuarial study requirement in this section.
17 Providers exempt pursuant to this subsection shall submit to the Commissioner, at least once
18 every five years, an actuarial projection of future population flows and adult care home bed and
19 nursing bed needs using appropriate mortality, morbidity, withdrawal, occupancy, and other
20 demographic assumptions and using a projection period that extends to a point at which, in the
21 actuary's professional judgment, the use of a longer period would not materially affect the results
22 and conclusions. The Commissioner may require an actuarial projection of future population
23 flows and adult care home bed and nursing bed needs sooner if there has been an increase or
24 decrease of twenty percent (20%) or more of one or more types of living units at a continuing
25 care retirement community during the provider's most recent fiscal year.
26 "§ 58-64A-215. Additional reporting.
27 If the Commissioner determines that additional information is needed to properly monitor the
28 financial condition or operations of a provider or continuing care retirement community or is
29 otherwise needed to protect the interests of residents and the general public, the Commissioner
30 may require a provider licensed under this Article to file any of the following:
31 (1) Monthly unaudited financial statements in the format required by
32 G.S. 58-64A-205 which shall be due no later than 45 days after the end of
33 each month.
34 (2) Any other data, financial statements, and pertinent information as the
35 Commissioner may reasonably require regarding (i) the provider, (ii) the
36 provider's obligated group, (iii) the continuing care retirement community, or
37 (iv) any related party, if the provider relies on a contractual or financial
38 relationship with the related party in order to meet the financial requirements
39 of this Article, or has a material amount invested in, or has a material amount
40 of receivables due from, the related party.
41 "Part 9. Notification Requirements.
42 "§ 58-64A-220. Notifications to Commissioner and residents.
43 A provider shall notify the Commissioner and all residents in writing within 10 business days
44 whenever any of the following apply:
45 (1) The provider fails to maintain the operating reserve required pursuant to Part
46 11 of this Article.
47 (2) The provider, or any obligated group of which the provider is a member,
48 violates or seeks modification, waiver, or extension of any material covenant
49 or material payment terms contained in any debt agreement.
50 (3) The provider has any entrance fee refunds that become more than 30 days
51 contractually past due.
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 39

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (4) The provider plans to reduce the number of any type of living unit by twenty
2 percent (20%) or more. The notification shall include a statement describing
3 the reasons for the reduction and the effect, if any, on residents and the
4 financial condition of the provider. For the purposes of this subdivision, the
5 percentage shall be based on the type of living unit being reduced.
6 (5) The provider makes any change to its name, or the name of a continuing care
7 retirement community operated by the provider in this State, including the
8 adoption of an assumed business name.
9 (6) Any proceeding for denial, suspension, or revocation of any license or permit
10 needed to operate all or part of a continuing care retirement community in this
11 State.
12 "§ 58-64A-225. Material changes or deviations in information.
13 (a) An applicant or provider shall notify the Commissioner of material changes or
14 deviations in any information submitted to the Commissioner pursuant to this Article within 10
15 business days after the applicant or provider becomes aware of the change or deviation.
16 (b) Within 30 days after receiving notice of a material change or deviation, the
17 Commissioner shall advise the applicant or provider in writing whether any additional action
18 needs to be taken as a result of the material change or deviation.
19 (c) The Commissioner may suspend any approval, certification, license, or permit issued
20 pursuant to this Article if the applicant or provider fails to give written notice of material changes
21 or deviations required by this section. The suspension shall remain in effect until the
22 Commissioner has (i) assessed the potential impact of the material changes or deviations on the
23 applicant or provider and the interests of residents and depositors and (ii) taken any action
24 necessary under this Article to protect the interests of any residents and depositors.
25 (d) For the purposes of this section, material changes or deviations mean any change or
26 extraordinary occurrence which creates or causes, or could create or cause, an applicant or
27 provider to be in a hazardous condition or, for a proposed continuing care retirement community
28 or proposed expansion of a continuing care retirement community, to no longer be financially
29 viable.
30 "Part 10. Other Transactions and Changes.
31 "§ 58-64A-230. Purchase, sale, or transfer of ownership interest in the real property of a
32 continuing care retirement community.
33 (a) No permit, certificate, or license issued pursuant to this Article is transferable, and no
34 permit, certificate, or license issued pursuant to this Article has value for sale or exchange as
35 property.
36 (b) A provider or any other person who owns the real property used in the operations of
37 a continuing care retirement community shall obtain approval from the Commissioner before
38 consummating any sale or transfer of any real property used in the operations of a continuing
39 care retirement community, including a sale-leaseback transaction, or any interest in a continuing
40 care retirement community, other than the sale of an independent living unit to a resident or other
41 transferee.
42 (c) A provider shall obtain approval from the Commissioner before consummating any
43 purchase of real property currently leased and used by the provider in the operations of a
44 continuing care retirement community. Any purchase option to be entered into by the provider
45 that requires a purchase option deposit shall only be entered into if the deposit is placed in an
46 escrow account or secured in another method acceptable to the Commissioner.
47 (d) A provider shall request approval of any transaction listed in subsection (b) or (c) of
48 this section by filing a request for approval with the Commissioner, made under oath or
49 affirmation, at least 45 days prior to consummating the transaction. The request for approval
50 required by this subsection shall include all of the following:
51 (1) The identity and description of the persons involved in the transaction.
Page 40 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (2) A description of the transaction and the terms of the transaction.
2 (3) A description of the financial impact on the applicant.
3 (4) If applicable, a plan for ensuring performance of existing continuing care and
4 continuing care at home contract obligations.
5 (5) Any other information reasonably required by the Commissioner.
6 (e) The Commissioner shall comply with the review schedule in G.S. 58-64A-70 in
7 response to a request for approval pursuant to this section.
8 (f) The Commissioner shall approve a request for approval if all of the following
9 requirements are met:
10 (1) The request complies with this section.
11 (2) None of the grounds for denial listed in G.S. 58-64A-280 apply to the
12 applicant.

14 prejudice the interest of residents.
15 (g) A provider shall give written notice to all affected residents and depositors of the
16 proposed transaction within 10 business days after receiving approval from the Commissioner.
17 (h) The Commissioner may revoke or restrict the certificate or license of a provider or
18 take other administrative action pursuant to Part 12 of this Article if a provider violates the
19 provisions of this section.
20 "§ 58-64A-235. Change of control of a provider.
21 (a) No person shall enter into an agreement to merge with, or to otherwise acquire control
22 of, a provider holding a certificate or license under this Article unless the transaction is approved
23 by the Commissioner. To obtain the Commissioner's approval, the acquiring person shall file a
24 request for approval with the Commissioner.
25 (b) The request for approval required by this section shall be in a form prescribed by the
26 Commissioner, made under oath or affirmation, and shall contain all of the following
27 information:
28 (1) The name and address of each acquiring person and the following additional
29 information regarding those persons:
30 a. If the person is not an individual, a report of the nature of its business
31 operations during the past five years or for a lesser period as the person
32 and any predecessors have been in existence.
33 b. A description of the business intended to be done by the person and
34 the person's related parties.
35 c. A list of all individuals who are or who have been selected to become
36 directors or executive officers of the person, or who perform or will
37 perform functions appropriate to those positions.
38 d. For each individual listed pursuant to this subdivision, the person's
39 principal occupation and all offices and positions held during the past
40 five years and any conviction of crimes other than minor traffic
41 violations during the past 10 years.
42 (2) The source, nature, and amount of the consideration used or to be used in
43 effecting the merger or other acquisition of control; a description of any
44 transaction wherein funds were or are to be obtained for that purpose,
45 including any pledge of the provider's stock, or the stock of any of its
46 subsidiaries or controlling persons; and the identity of persons providing the
47 consideration.
48 (3) Fully audited financial information as to the earnings and financial condition
49 of each acquiring person for the preceding five fiscal years, or for a lesser
50 period as the acquiring person and any predecessors have been in existence,
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 41

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 and similar unaudited information as of a date not earlier than 90 days prior
2 to the filing of the written notice.
3 (4) Any plans or proposals that each acquiring person may have to liquidate the
4 provider, or any continuing care retirement community operated by the
5 provider in this State, to sell its assets or merge or consolidate it with any
6 person, or to make any other material change in its business or corporate
7 structure or management.
8 (5) A description of the effect, if any, that the merger or other acquisition of
9 control will have on the financial condition of the provider.
10 (6) A description of any change in the provision of goods and services to the
11 provider and residents.
12 (7) A description of any agreements made or to be made with residents which will

15 (8) A description of any service or contractual obligation with residents which

17 (9) Any additional information as the Commissioner may require as necessary or
18 appropriate for the protection of residents or in the public interest.
19 (c) The Commissioner shall comply with the review schedule in G.S. 58-64A-70 in
20 response to a request for approval pursuant to this section.
21 (d) The Commissioner shall approve a request for approval pursuant to this section if all
22 of the following requirements are met:
23 (1) The request for approval complies with this section.
24 (2) None of the grounds for denial listed in G.S. 58-64A-280 apply to the

26 (3) After the change of control, the provider will be able to satisfy the certification
27 or licensure requirements, as applicable, of this Article.
28 (4) The financial condition of any acquiring person will not jeopardize the
29 financial stability of the provider or prejudice the interest of any residents.
30 (5) Any plans or proposals that any acquiring person has to liquidate the provider,
31 or any continuing care retirement community operated by the provider in this
32 State, sell its assets or consolidate or merge it with any person, or to make any
33 other material change in its business or corporate structure or management,
34 are fair and reasonable to residents and in the public interest.
35 (6) The competence, experience, and integrity of those persons who would
36 control the operation of the provider are such that the change of control will
37 not harm the interests of residents or of the public.
38 (e) A provider shall give written notice to all affected residents and depositors of the
39 proposed merger or other acquisition of control within 10 business days after the acquiring person
40 has received approval from the Commissioner.
41 (f) The Commissioner may revoke or restrict the license or certificate of a provider or
42 take other administrative action pursuant to Part 12 of this Article if a provider violates the
43 provisions of this section.
44 "§ 58-64A-240. Third-party management.
45 (a) A provider shall request the approval of the Commissioner before entering into a
46 contract with a third party for the management of a continuing care retirement community. The
47 request for approval required by this section shall include a copy of the proposed management
48 contract, the information required by subdivisions (6) and (7) of G.S. 58-64A-150(a) regarding
49 the proposed third-party manager, a description of the third party's experience in managing
50 continuing care retirement communities, and the reason for the change in management.
Page 42 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (b) The provider shall inform all residents in writing of the request for approval submitted
2 to the Commissioner pursuant to this section within 10 business days after the request for
3 approval is submitted to the Commissioner.
4 (c) The Commissioner shall comply with the review schedule in G.S. 58-64A-70 in
5 response to a request for approval pursuant to this section.
6 (d) The Commissioner may disapprove of the request for approval if the Commissioner
7 determines either of the following:
8 (1) The proposed third-party manager is incompetent or untrustworthy or so
9 lacking in managerial experience as to make the operation of the continuing
10 care retirement community potentially hazardous to residents.
11 (2) The proposed third-party manager is affiliated directly or indirectly through
12 ownership, control, or business relations with any person or persons whose
13 business operations are or have been marked by manipulation of assets or
14 accounts or by bad faith, to the detriment of residents, members, stockholders,
15 investors, creditors, or the public.
16 (e) The provider shall remove any third-party manager immediately upon discovery of
17 either of the following:
18 (1) That a manager has been convicted of any felony or pleaded nolo contendere
19 to a felony charge or has been held liable or enjoined in a civil action by final
20 judgment involving fraud, embezzlement, fraudulent conversion, or
21 misappropriation of property.
22 (2) That a manager is now, or was in the past, affiliated directly or indirectly
23 through ownership interest of ten percent (10%) or more in, or control of, any
24 business, corporation, or other entity that has been convicted of any felony or
25 pleaded nolo contendere to a felony charge or has been held liable or enjoined
26 in a civil action by final judgment involving fraud, embezzlement, fraudulent
27 conversion, or misappropriation of property.
28 "Part 11. Operating Reserve.
29 "§ 58-64A-245. Operating reserve requirement.
30 (a) A provider shall maintain after the opening of a continuing care retirement
31 community an operating reserve equal to fifty percent (50%) of the total operating costs of the
32 continuing care retirement community forecasted or projected for the 12-month period following
33 the period covered by the most recent disclosure statement filed with the Department.
34 (b) Once a continuing care retirement community achieves a 12-month daily average
35 independent living unit occupancy rate of ninety percent (90%) or higher, a provider shall only
36 be required to maintain an operating reserve in an amount calculated using the table below, unless
37 otherwise instructed by the Commissioner:
38 12-Month Daily Average Operating Reserve Requirement as a Percentage
39 Independent Living Unit of Total Operating Costs of the Continuing Care
40 Occupancy Rate Retirement Community
41 90% or above..................................................................................................................... 25.00%
42 86% to 89.9% .................................................................................................................... 31.25%
43 83% to 85.9% .................................................................................................................... 37.50%
44 80% to 82.9% .................................................................................................................... 43.75%
45 Below 80% ........................................................................................................................ 50.00%
46 (c) A provider who has a 12-month daily average independent living unit occupancy rate
47 equal to or in excess of ninety-three percent (93%) and has no long-term debt or a debt service
48 coverage ratio in excess of 2.00 as of the provider's most recent fiscal year-end shall only be
49 required to maintain an operating reserve equal to twelve and one-half percent (12.5%) of total
50 operating costs of the continuing care retirement community, unless otherwise instructed by the
51 Commissioner.
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 43

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (d) The Commissioner may increase the amount a provider is required to maintain as its
2 operating reserve, not to exceed fifty percent (50%) of total operating costs as calculated in
3 accordance with G.S. 58-64A-250, for a continuing care retirement community operated by the
4 provider or require that a provider immediately place the operating reserve on deposit with the
5 Commissioner if the Commissioner has determined that the provider is in a hazardous condition
6 pursuant to G.S. 58-64A-285.
7 (e) A provider shall notify all residents in writing within 10 business days if the
8 Commissioner, pursuant to subsection (d) of this section, increases the amount a provider is
9 required to maintain as its operating reserve for a continuing care retirement community operated
10 by the provider or requires the operating reserve to be placed on deposit with the Commissioner.
11 (f) If the Commissioner requires a provider to place an operating reserve on deposit with
12 the Commissioner, the provider shall at the same time deliver to the Commissioner a power of
13 attorney executed by the provider's president and secretary, or other proper person or persons,
14 authorizing the sale or transfer of said qualifying assets, or any part, for the purpose of paying
15 any of the liabilities of the provider related to the continuing care retirement community for
16 which the operating reserve is maintained.
17 "§ 58-64A-250. Operating reserve calculation.
18 (a) The five-year prospective financial statements as required by
19 G.S. 58-64A-150(a)(37), together with the 12-month daily average independent living unit
20 occupancy rate of the continuing care retirement community, shall serve as the basis for
21 computing the operating reserve. A provider shall calculate and adjust, if necessary, the required
22 operating reserve on at least a semiannual basis, including the date the operating reserve is
23 certified in accordance with G.S. 58-64A-270.
24 (b) In addition to total operating expenses, total operating costs will include debt service,
25 consisting of principal and interest payments, along with taxes and insurance on any mortgage
26 loan or other long-term financing, but will exclude depreciation, amortized expenses, and
27 extraordinary items as approved by the Commissioner. If the debt service portion is accounted
28 for by way of another reserve account, the debt service portion may be excluded upon satisfactory
29 evidence of the existence and purpose of the other reserve account.
30 (c) A provider shall apply in writing for a determination by the Commissioner in order
31 to exclude extraordinary items from total operating costs and shall provide documentation to
32 support the request. The Commissioner shall comply with the review schedule in G.S. 58-64A-70
33 in response to a request for approval pursuant to this subsection.
34 (d) For providers that have voluntarily and permanently discontinued entering into
35 continuing care contracts, or who operate a continuing care retirement community where not all
36 occupants are under continuing care contracts, the Commissioner may allow a reduced operating
37 reserve if the Commissioner finds that the reduction is consistent with the financial protections
38 imposed by this Article. In making this determination, the Commissioner may consider factors
39 including the financial condition of the provider, the number of outstanding continuing care
40 contracts, the ratio of persons under continuing care contracts to those persons who do not hold
41 a continuing care contract, and the 12-month daily average independent living unit occupancy
42 rate.
43 (e) A provider who has increased the number of independent living units available at a
44 continuing care retirement community in excess of twenty percent (20%) shall be allowed to
45 exclude the total number of independent living units in the expansion project for a period of 18
46 months after the independent living units become available for occupancy when computing the
47 operating reserve required by this Part.
48 (f) The Commissioner may allow a different calculation for a provider's required
49 operating reserve for a continuing care retirement community operated by the provider if the
50 calculation, in the opinion of the Commissioner, does not diminish the residents' protections
51 provided for by this Part.
Page 44 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 "§ 58-64A-255. Qualifying assets.
2 (a) A provider shall fund its operating reserve with any of the following qualifying assets:
3 (1) Cash.
4 (2) Cash equivalents.
5 (3) Investment grade securities. For the purposes of this subdivision, investment
6 grade securities are any of the following:
7 a. Securities issued or directly and fully guaranteed or insured by the
8 government of the United States of America or any of its agencies or
9 instrumentalities.
10 b. Debt securities or debt instruments with a rating of BBB- or higher by
11 Standard & Poor's or Baa3 or higher by Moody's, or, if no rating of
12 Standard & Poor's or Moody's then exists, the equivalent of that rating
13 by any other nationally recognized statistical rating organizations
14 maintained by the National Association of Insurance Commissioners.
15 c. Investments in any fund that invests exclusively in investments of the
16 type described in sub-subdivision a. or b. of this subdivision, which
17 fund may also hold immaterial amounts of cash pending investment or
18 distribution.
19 (4) Corporate stock that is traded on a public securities exchange that can be
20 readily valued and liquidated for cash, including shares in mutual funds and
21 exchange-traded funds that hold portfolios consisting predominantly of these
22 stocks.
23 (5) Other assets considered to be acceptable to the Commissioner on a
24 case-by-case basis.
25 (b) Except as otherwise provided in this subsection, the assets maintained by the provider
26 as an operating reserve for a continuing care retirement community operated by the provider
27 under this Article shall not be subject to any liens, charges, judgments, garnishments, or creditors'
28 claims and shall not be hypothecated, pledged as collateral, or otherwise encumbered in any
29 manner. A provider may encumber assets held as an operating reserve as part of a security pledge
30 of assets or similar collateralization that is part of the provider's debt financing and is included
31 in the provider's debt indenture security instruments related thereto or other similar instrument.
32 (c) For the purpose of calculating the amount to be maintained by the provider to satisfy
33 its operating reserve requirement, all qualifying assets shall be valued at their current fair market
34 value.
35 "§ 58-64A-260. Surety bond; letter of credit.
36 (a) Alternative Funding Methods. – In lieu of funding the operating reserve with
37 qualifying assets as set forth in G.S. 58-64A-255, a provider may fund all or a portion of the
38 operating reserve required by this Part by filing with the Commissioner a surety bond or letter of
39 credit as set forth in this section.
40 (b) Surety Bond. – A surety bond shall be in a form acceptable to the Commissioner and
41 issued by an insurer authorized by the Commissioner to write surety business in this State. All of
42 the following shall apply to surety bonds issued pursuant to this Article:
43 (1) The surety bond may be exchanged or replaced with another surety bond if (i)
44 the surety bond applies to obligations and liabilities that arose during the
45 period of the original surety bond, (ii) the surety bond meets the requirements
46 of this section, and (iii) 90 days' advance written notice is provided to the
47 Commissioner.
48 (2) Notice of cancellation or nonrenewal of the surety bond required by this
49 section shall be provided to the provider and the Commissioner in writing at
50 least 45 days before cancellation or nonrenewal.
Senate Bill 105-First Edition Page 45

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (3) A surety bond may be canceled by the issuer of the bond with respect to future
2 obligations or liabilities upon proper notice pursuant to this section and
3 without regard to approval or acceptance of the Commissioner.
4 (c) Letter of Credit. – A provider may file a clean, irrevocable, unconditional letter of
5 credit issued or confirmed by a qualified United States financial institution as defined in
6 G.S. 58-7-26(b) naming the Commissioner as beneficiary. The terms of the letter of credit shall
7 be approved by the Commissioner before issuance and before its renewal or modification. The
8 letter of credit shall provide all of the following information:
9 (1) Ninety days' prior written notice to both the provider and the Commissioner
10 of the financial institution's determination not to renew or extend the term of
11 the letter of credit.
12 (2) Unless otherwise arranged by the provider to the satisfaction of the
13 Commissioner, deposit by the financial institution of letter of credit funds in
14 an account designated by the Commissioner no later than 30 days before the
15 expiration of the letter of credit.
16 (3) Deposit by the financial institution of letter of credit funds in an account
17 designated by the Commissioner within five business days following written
18 instructions from the Commissioner that, in the sole judgment of the
19 Commissioner, funding of the operating reserve is required.
20 "§ 58-64A-265. Operating reserve release.
21 (a) An operating reserve shall only be released, in whole or in part, upon the submittal of
22 a detailed request from the provider and approval of that request by the Commissioner. This
23 request shall be submitted in writing for the Commissioner to review at least 10 business days
24 prior to the proposed date of release.
25 (b) In order to receive the approval of the Commissioner, a provider shall explain why a
26 release is necessary and, if applicable, submit a repayment schedule to replenish the operating
27 reserve to the amount required by G.S. 58-64A-245. Within five business days after the date a
28 request is deemed complete, the Commissioner shall provide the provider with a written notice
29 of approval or disapproval of the request. The Commissioner may disapprove any request to
30 release the funds if it is determined that the release is not in the best interest of residents.
31 (c) A provider shall give written notice to residents of any request made pursuant to
32 subsection (a) of this section at the same time the written request is submitted to the
33 Commissioner.
34 "§ 58-64A-270. Operating reserve certification.
35 At the time a provider files its annual audited financial statements pursuant to
36 G.S. 58-64A-195, a provider shall file a form acceptable to the Commissioner computing,
37 reporting, and certifying all of the following:
38 (1) The 12-month daily average independent living unit occupancy rate at the
39 continuing care retirement community, or a shorter period of time that the
40 continuing care retirement community has been in operation, as of the date of
41 certification.
42 (2) The amount the provider is required to hold as its operating reserve.
43 (3) A description of the qualifying assets or other form of security and, if
44 applicable, their respective values, as defined and valued in accordance with
45 G.S. 58-64A-255, that the provider maintains for its operating reserve.
46 "Part 12. Offenses and Penalties.
47 "§ 58-64A-275. Definition of impairment.
48 As used is this Part, "impaired" means a weakened financial state or condition that may affect
49 a provider's ability to pay its obligations as they come due in the normal course of business.
50 "§ 58-64A-280. Grounds for discretionary refusal, restriction, or revocation of a permit,
51 certificate, or license.
Page 46 Senate Bill 105-First Edition

General Assembly Of North Carolina Session 2025
1 (a) The Commissioner may (i) deny an application or any other request for approval or
2 (ii) restrict or revoke any permit, certificate, license, or other authorization issued under this
3 Article if the Commissioner finds that the applicant or provider did any of the following:
4 (1) Willfully violated any provision of this Article or of any rule or order of the
5 Commissioner.
6 (2) Made a material omission, misstatement, or misrepresentation, or committed
7 fraud in obtaining a permit, certificate, license, or other authorization.
8 (3) Engaged in any fraudulent or dishonest practices in the conduct of its business.
9 (4) Misappropriated, converted, or improperly withheld any monies.
10 (5) Failed to file an annual disclosure statement, annual audited financial
11 statements, or any other materials requested by the Commissioner or
12 otherwise required by this Article.
13 (6) Failed to deliver to prospective residents a disclosure statement as required by
14 this Article.
15 (7) Delivered to prospective residents a disclosure statement that makes a material
16 misstatement or omits a material fact and the provider, at the time of the
17 delivery of the disclosure statement, had actual knowledge of the misstatement
18 or omission.
19 (8) Failed to make a revised disclosure statement available to residents.
20 (9) Made any material misrepresentations to depositors, prospective residents, or
21 residents of a continuing care retirement community operated or to be
22 operated in this State.
23 (10) Failed to maintain the escrow account required under this Article or released
24 a portion of an escrow account required to be maintained under this Article.
25 (11) Failed to deposit entrance fees and deposits into an escrow account as required
26 by this Article.
27 (12) Failed to maintain the operating reserve required under this Article or released
28 a portion of the operating reserve required to be maintained under this Article
29 without Commissioner approval.
30 (13) Violated a restriction of its permit, certificate, or license.
31 (14) After request by the Commissioner for an investigation or examination,
32 refused access to records or information; refused to be investigated or
33 examined or to produce its accounts, records, and files for an investigation or
34 examination; refused to give information with respect to its affairs; or refused
35 to perform any other legal obligations related to an investigation or
36 examination.
37 (15) Failed to fulfill obligations under continuing care and continuing care at home
38 contracts.
39 (16) Violated the provisions of G.S. 58-64A-230, 58-64A-235, or 58-64A-240.
40 (17) Failed to comply with the terms of a cease and desist order.
41 (18) Has been determined by the Commissioner to be in a hazardous condition.
42 (b) Findings of fact in support of a denial, restriction, or revocation shall be accompanied
43 by an explicit statement of the Commissioner's understanding of the underlying facts supporting
44 the findings.
45 (c) If the Commissioner has good cause to believe that a provider has committed a
46 violation for which revocation could be ordered, the Commissioner may first issue a cease and
47 desist order. If the cease and desist order is not or cannot be effective in remedying the violation,
48 the Commissioner may, after notice and hearing, order that a permit, certificate, or license be
49 revoked. That revocation order may be appealed to the Superior Court of Wake County in the
50 manner provided by G.S. 58-63-35. The provider shall accept no new deposits or entrance fees
51 while the revocation order is under appeal.

1 (d) If the Commissioner issues a cease and desist order or restricts or revokes a provider's
2 permit, certificate, or license, the provider shall notify all residents and depositors of the cease
3 and desist order, restriction, or revocation within five business days.
4 (e) The Commissioner may, upon finding of changed circumstances, remove a
